It provides:\n\n1. **Resource Isolation**: Prevents pods from exceeding allocated resources\n2. **QoS Enforcement**: Implements Kubernetes QoS tiers (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort) with distinct CPU and memory behavior\n3. **Topology Optimization**: Aligns container resources to hardware topology (NUMA nodes) for optimal performance\n4. **Device Management**: Brokers extended resources (GPUs, accelerators) reported by device plugins\n5. **Admission Control**: Rejects pods that violate topology constraints before container creation\n6. **Node Accounting**: Tracks system resource consumption and ensures node allocatable is respected\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies** (What feeds into this subsystem):\n- **Pod Specification** (`v1.Pod`): CPU/memory requests and limits, QoS class, device plugin resource requests\n- **Node Specification** (`v1.Node`): Capacity, allocatable, extended resource counts\n- **Runtime Service** (`internalapi.RuntimeService`): Container startup notifications, actual container limits\n- **Active Pods Callback** (`ActivePodsFunc`): Current running pods for recalculation\n- **Plugin Manager**: Device plugin registration and health status\n\n**Downstream Consumers** (What this subsystem affects):\n- **Container Runtime** (CRI): Container execution with configured cpuset, memory limits via `RunContainerOptions`\n- **Cgroup Filesystem**: Direct manipulation via cgroup manager for resource limits\n- **Kubelet Status Module**: Pod resource status via `PodResources` API and allocated resources\n- **Scheduler Framework**: Topology hints inform scheduler pod placement decisions\n- **Kubelet Metrics**: CPU/memory usage from cAdvisor integration\n\n### Architectural Constraints\n\n- **Per-Node Scope**: Operates only on the local node; no inter-node coordination\n- **Immutable Pod QoS**: QoS class is determined once during pod creation based on requests/limits, not updated\n- **Best-Effort Reconciliation**: Periodic (1-minute) updates ensure desired vs. actual state; no per-container hooks\n- **Cgroup Version Coupling**: Behavior differs significantly between cgroup v1 and v2 with separate code paths\n- **Linux-Primary Design**: Most functionality (CPU/memory managers, QOS tiers) is Linux-only; Windows is minimal\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Central Orchestrator: containerManagerImpl\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` (lines 100-140)\n\nThe `containerManagerImpl` struct is the central hub managing lifecycle and delegation:\n\n```go\ntype containerManagerImpl struct {\n    sync.RWMutex\n    // Infrastructure\n    cadvisorInterface cadvisor.Interface\n    cgroupManager CgroupManager\n    nodeInfo *v1.Node\n    systemContainers []*systemContainer\n\n    // Configuration\n    NodeConfig\n    subsystems *CgroupSubsystems\n    cgroupRoot CgroupName\n\n    // State and Capacity\n    capacity v1.ResourceList\n    internalCapacity v1.ResourceList\n\n    // Sub-managers for resource coordination\n    qosContainerManager QOSContainerManager\n    deviceManager devicemanager.Manager\n    cpuManager cpumanager.Manager\n    memoryManager memorymanager.Manager\n    topologyManager topologymanager.Manager\n    draManager *dra.Manager\n\n    // Event distribution\n    recorder record.EventRecorder\n    resourceUpdates chan resourceupdates.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Responsibilities**:\n1. Initialize and start all sub-managers during node setup\n2. Provide facade methods for capacity reporting (`GetCapacity`, `GetNodeAllocatableReservation`)\n3. Distribute admission decisions via topology manager\n4. Route dynamic resource changes to consumers via `resourceUpdates` channel\n5. Implement `InternalContainerLifecycle` hooks for resource pre-configuration\n\n### 2.2 Sub-Manager Components\n\n#### A. CPU Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: CPU affinity assignment and exclusive CPU allocation\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Start()`: Load existing allocations from checkpoint\n- `AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)`: Assign CPUs and record decision\n- `GetCPUAffinity(podUID, containerName) cpuset.CPUSet`: Return CPU assignment\n- `GetExclusiveCPUs(podUID, containerName) cpuset.CPUSet`: Query for PodResources API\n\n**Policies**:\n- `none`: No assignment, container uses all CPUs\n- `static`: Bind exclusive containers to specific CPUs (deterministic allocation from reserved CPUs)\n- Both policies respect `reserved` CPUs (system, kube-reserved) and isolated CPUs (via topology manager hints)\n\n**Failure Mode**:\n- If static policy cannot find contiguous CPU set for exclusive container → returns error\n- Pod stays pending until CPUs available or request modified\n\n#### B. Memory Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: NUMA-aware memory allocation and huge page configuration\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Start()`: Detect NUMA topology and restore allocations\n- `AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)`: Allocate NUMA nodes\n- `GetTopologyHints()`: Provide NUMA hints to topology manager\n\n**Policies**:\n- `none`: No NUMA affinity, container can access all memory\n- `static`: Bind containers to specific NUMA nodes\n- `best-effort`: Allocate from single NUMA node if possible, else multi-node\n\n**State Persistence**: Checkpoint file at `<kubelet-root>/cpu_manager_state`\n\n#### C. Topology Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Coordinate topology affinity across all hint providers; enforce policies during pod admission\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Admit(attrs *lifecycle.PodAdmitAttributes) lifecycle.PodAdmitResult`: Gating function for pod acceptance\n- `GetTopologyHints(pod, container) []NUMATopologyHint`: Query hint providers for alignment options\n- `AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)`: Record topology assignment\n- `RemoveContainer(containerID)`: Clean up tracking\n\n**Policies**:\n- `none`: No enforcement (all pods admitted)\n- `best-effort`: Prefers aligned topology but admits misaligned pods\n- `restricted`: Rejects misaligned pods (only admits if all hints agree on NUMA nodes)\n- `single-numa-node`: All containers in pod must fit on single NUMA node\n\n**Scope**:\n- `pod`: Aggregate hints across all containers, one decision per pod\n- `container`: Each container evaluated independently\n\n**Admission Decision Flow**:\n```\nPod Arrival\n  ↓\nTopology Manager.Admit()\n  ├─ Query CPU Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n  ├─ Query Memory Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n  ├─ Query Device Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n  ├─ Aggregate hints using policy\n  ├─ Check if feasible combination exists\n  └─ Return Accept or Reject\n```\n\n#### D. Device Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Manage extended resources (GPUs, accelerators); broker device plugin allocation\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `Start()`: Discover devices and watch plugin registration endpoints\n- `Allocate(pod, container, requests): error`: Allocate devices via plugin Allocate RPC\n- `GetDevicePluginResourceCapacity(): (capacity, allocatable, inactive)`: Report resource counts\n- `GetTopologyHints(pod, container): []hints`: Provide NUMA topology hints if devices are NUMA-aware\n- `Updates() <-chan resourceupdates.Update`: Broadcast device health changes\n\n**Device Plugin Integration**:\n- Uses Unix socket discovery (`/var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/`)\n- Implements both v1beta1 (legacy) and v1 (current) plugin APIs\n- Tracks allocation state per pod for recovery on restart\n\n**State Persistence**: Device allocation checkpoint at `<kubelet-root>/device-plugin-state`\n\n#### E. Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Manage ResourceClaims (Kubernetes 1.26+); prepare and unprepare dynamic resources\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `PrepareDynamicResources(ctx, pod)`: Claim resources from ResourceClaim specs\n- `UnprepareDynamicResources(ctx, pod)`: Release claimed resources\n- `GetTopologyHints(pod, container)`: Provide topology hints based on claimed resources\n- `Updates() <-chan resourceupdates.Update`: Broadcast unavailable claims\n\n**Resource Claim Lifecycle**:\n```\nPod with ResourceClaim Spec\n  ↓\nPrepareDynamicResources()\n  ├─ Call resource driver's Prepare RPC\n  ├─ Wait for ResourceClaim status.AllocationResult\n  ├─ Record claim allocation\n  └─ Return CDI device specs to container runtime\n  ↓\nContainer Created with CDI devices\n  ↓\nPod Deletion\n  ↓\nUnprepareDynamicResources()\n  ├─ Call resource driver's Unprepare RPC\n  └─ Clean up claim state\n```\n\n**Failure Handling**: If claim becomes unavailable mid-pod-life, sends update → kubelet can evict pod\n\n#### F. QoS Container Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Manage top-level QoS-tier cgroups and enforce per-tier resource policies\n\n**QoS Tiers**:\n- **Guaranteed**: Pods with requests == limits; highest priority; full CPU access when not contested\n- **Burstable**: Pods with requests but no limits; medium priority; CPU shares proportional to requests\n- **BestEffort**: Pods with neither requests nor limits; lowest priority; killed first under pressure\n\n**Resource Configuration**:\n- **CPU Shares**:\n  - Guaranteed: Unlimited (no shares limit)\n  - Burstable: Sum of all pod requests converted via `MilliCPUToShares()`: `(milliCPU * 1024) / 1000` with `Min=2, Max=262144`\n  - BestEffort: 2 shares (kernel minimum)\n- **Memory**: Applied per-pod under QoS tier parent\n- **Memory QoS** (cgroup v2 only):\n  - Sets `memory.min` for burstable and guaranteed tiers\n  - Protects these pods from memory pressure\n\n**Periodic Update**: Every 60 seconds (`periodicQOSCgroupUpdateInterval`) via `UpdateQOSCgroups()`\n\n**CPU Quota Override**: If `DisableCPUQuotaWithExclusiveCPUs` feature enabled and pod has exclusive CPUs, CPU limits (quota) disabled\n\n#### G. Pod Container Manager\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Create and manage pod-level cgroups within QoS tiers\n\n**Hierarchy**:\n```\nQoSContainer (Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort)\n└── Pod Cgroup (kubepods.burstable.podXXX)\n    └── Container cgroup (created by runtime with cpuset, memory)\n```\n\n**Key Methods**:\n- `EnsureExists(pod)`: Create pod cgroup with CPU/memory config\n- `GetPodContainerName(pod)`: Compute cgroup name from QoS class\n- `Destroy(podCgroupName)`: Remove pod cgroup\n- `IsPodCgroup(cgroupfsName): (bool, types.UID)`: Check if cgroupfs path is a pod\n\n**Pod Cgroup Configuration** (via `ResourceConfigForPod()`):\n- CPU shares from pod requests, adjusted for QoS tier\n- Memory limit = pod requests (or limits if present)\n- CPU quota only if `enforceCPULimits=true` (can disable for exclusive CPUs)\n- Huge page limits from pod resource specs\n\n#### H. Cgroup Manager (Linux)\n\n**Location**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` (dispatcher), `cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go`, `cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go`\n\n**Responsibility**: Abstract cgroup filesystem or systemd interface for Create/Update/Destroy operations\n\n**Implementation Options**:\n- **cgroupv1impl**: Direct cgroup filesystem manipulation (`/sys/fs/cgroup/...`)\n- **cgroupv2impl**: Unified cgroup v2 hierarchy with single write path\n- **Systemd Driver**: Uses systemd unit files (slices) instead of direct filesystem\n\n**Interface** (from `types.go`):\n```go\ntype CgroupManager interface {\n    Create(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Update(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Destroy(logger klog.Logger, config *CgroupConfig) error\n    Exists(name CgroupName) bool\n    Name(name CgroupName) string        // Internal → cgroupfs\n    Pids(logger klog.Logger, name CgroupName) []int\n    MemoryUsage(name CgroupName) (int64, error)\n    GetCgroupConfig(name CgroupName, resource v1.ResourceName) (*ResourceConfig, error)\n    Version() int                        // 1 or 2\n}\n```\n\n**Key Resource Parameters** (ResourceConfig):\n- `Memory`: Limit in bytes (memory.limit_in_bytes or memory.max)\n- `CPUSet`: CPUs accessible (cpuset.cpus)\n- `CPUShares`: CPU relative weight (cpu.shares)\n- `CPUQuota`: Hard CPU limit in microseconds (cpu.cfs_quota_us)\n- `PidsLimit`: Max process count (pids.max)\n- `Unified`: cgroup v2-only settings (memory.min, memory.high, etc.)\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: End-to-End Control Flow with Concrete Evidence\n\n### 3.1 Container Manager Initialization\n\n**Entry Point**: `NewContainerManager()` in `container_manager_linux.go` (lines 207-392)\n\n```\nNewContainerManager()\n  ├─ 1. Detect mounted subsystems\n  │    └─ GetCgroupSubsystems() → CgroupSubsystems{cpu, memory, cpuset, ...}\n  │\n  ├─ 2. Validate requirements\n  │    ├─ Ensure cpu and memory subsystems mounted\n  │    └─ Log deprecation warning if cgroup v1 detected\n  │\n  ├─ 3. Create cgroup manager\n  │    └─ NewCgroupManager(cgroupDriver, cgroupVersion) → cgroupV1impl or cgroupV2impl\n  │\n  ├─ 4. Initialize topology manager (policy enforcement hub)\n  │    └─ NewTopologyManager(policy, scope, machineInfo)\n  │        └─ machineInfo from cAdvisor (NUMA topology)\n  │\n  ├─ 5. Initialize device manager (with topology hints)\n  │    └─ NewManagerImpl(topologyHints=topologyManager)\n  │\n  ├─ 6. Initialize CPU manager\n  │    └─ NewManager(cpuPolicy, nodeConfig.ReservedSystemCPUs)\n  │\n  ├─ 7. Initialize memory manager\n  │    └─ NewManager(memoryPolicy, nodeConfig.MemoryManagerReservedMemory)\n  │\n  ├─ 8. Initialize DRA manager (if feature enabled)\n  │    └─ NewManager(kubeClient, nodeConfig.NodeName)\n  │\n  ├─ 9. Register hint providers with topology manager\n  │    ├─ topologyManager.AddHintProvider(cpuManager)\n  │    ├─ topologyManager.AddHintProvider(memoryManager)\n  │    └─ topologyManager.AddHintProvider(deviceManager)\n  │\n  ├─ 10. Initialize QoS container manager\n  │     └─ NewQOSContainerManager(cgroupManager, cgroupsPerQOS)\n  │\n  ├─ 11. Create resource updates channel\n  │     └─ resourceUpdates = make(chan resourceupdates.Update, 10)\n  │\n  └─ 12. Fan-in resource update streams (concurrent goroutines)\n         ├─ deviceManager.Updates() → resourceUpdates\n         └─ draManager.Updates() → resourceUpdates\n```\n\n**Key Evidence**:\n- Lines 249-251: Topology manager initialized before managers that use it\n- Lines 272-280: Device and CPU managers added as hint providers\n- Lines 358-389: Fan-in pattern for resource updates with error handling per source\n\n### 3.2 Node Startup Flow\n\n**Entry Point**: `Start()` in `container_manager_linux.go` (lines 615-710)\n\nThis is called once per node lifecycle when kubelet starts:\n\n```\ncontainerManagerImpl.Start(ctx, node, activePodsFunc, getNodeFunc, ...)\n  │\n  ├─ 1. Build existing container map from runtime\n  │    └─ containerMap := buildContainerMap(pod, containers from cgroups)\n  │\n  ├─ 2. Initialize DRA manager with existing pods\n  │    └─ draManager.Start(activePodsFunc) for recovery\n  │\n  ├─ 3. Start CPU manager\n  │    └─ cpuManager.Start(activePodsFunc)\n  │        ├─ Load checkpoint from <kubelet-root>/cpu_manager_state\n  │        └─ Reconcile allocations, move escaped processes back to cpusets\n  │\n  ├─ 4. Start memory manager\n  │    └─ memoryManager.Start(activePodsFunc)\n  │        └─ Similar checkpoint loading and reconciliation\n  │\n  ├─ 5. Setup node (cgroup initialization and enforcement)\n  │    └─ setupNode() [covered below]\n  │\n  ├─ 6. Start device manager\n  │    └─ deviceManager.Start(pod-based resource cleanup)\n  │        └─ Watch /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/ for plugin registration\n  │\n  ├─ 7. Start health checkers for plugins\n  │    └─ GetHealthCheckers() → kubelet integrates with systemd watchdog\n  │\n  └─ 8. Start periodic tasks\n       ├─ cpu reconciliation (ongoing)\n       ├─ memory reconciliation (ongoing)\n       ├─ QoS resource updates (60s interval)\n       └─ System container enforcement (60s interval)\n```\n\n**Critical Phase: setupNode()** (lines 504-584):\n\n```\nsetupNode()\n  │\n  ├─ 1. Kernel tuning\n  │    ├─ Check kernel.sysrq allowed\n  │    ├─ Check vm.overcommit_memory\n  │    └─ Warn if protection defaults differ\n  │\n  ├─ 2. QoS tier cgroup creation (if CgroupsPerQOS=true)\n  │    ├─ Create /kubepods/burstable cgroup\n  │    ├─ Create /kubepods/besteffort cgroup\n  │    └─ Start QoS manager for periodic tier-level resource updates\n  │\n  ├─ 3. Create system container\n  │    ├─ Create systemCgroup if SystemCgroupsName specified\n  │    ├─ Periodically (60s) move non-pod processes there\n  │    └─ Prevent processes from escaping QoS hierarchy\n  │\n  ├─ 4. Create kubelet container\n  │    ├─ Allocate own cgroup if KubeletCgroupsName specified\n  │    ├─ Apply OOM score adjustment (KubeletOOMScoreAdj)\n  │    └─ Move kubelet process into cgroup (or track its cgroup)\n  │\n  ├─ 5. Enforce node allocatable\n  │    ├─ Create root pod cgroup (/kubepods)\n  │    ├─ Apply resource limits (CPU shares, memory)\n  │    └─ Enforce with retries if memory oversubscribed\n  │\n  └─ 6. Return Status with any soft requirement violations\n       └─ e.g., \"cgroup v1 is deprecated, use cgroup v2\"\n```\n\n**File Evidence**:\n- Lines 89-98: System container creation with `newSystemCgroups()`\n- Lines 512-530: Node allocatable cgroup creation and enforcement\n- Lines 532-558: System and kubelet container setup with periodic tasks\n- Lines 563-584: Resource reservation enforcement\n\n### 3.3 Pod Admission Flow (Pre-Container Creation)\n\n**Entry Point**: `GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()` returns the topology manager's Admit method\n\nCalled by kubelet's pod admission controller when a new pod arrives:\n\n```\nKubelet receives Pod Spec\n  ↓\nPod Admission Controller\n  ├─ Call handlers from containerManager.GetAllocateResourcesPodAdmitHandler()\n  │  └─ → Returns topology manager's Admit(PodAdmitAttributes)\n  │\n  └─ Topology Manager.Admit(attrs) [topologymanager.go]\n      │\n      ├─ 1. Determine scope (pod-scoped or container-scoped)\n      │    └─ Based on policy configuration\n      │\n      ├─ 2. Collect topology hints\n      │    ├─ For each container in pod:\n      │    │   ├─ CPU Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n      │    │   │  └─ Returns possible NUMA node sets for CPU allocation\n      │    │   ├─ Memory Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n      │    │   │  └─ Returns compatible NUMA nodes for memory\n      │    │   └─ Device Manager.GetTopologyHints(pod, container)\n      │    │      └─ Returns NUMA locality for allocated devices\n      │    │\n      │    └─ Collect hints per resource type (cpus, memory, devices, ...)\n      │\n      ├─ 3. Apply policy logic\n      │    ├─ Policy: none\n      │    │  └─ Accept all (no topology enforcement)\n      │    │\n      │    ├─ Policy: best-effort\n      │    │  ├─ Find intersection of all hint sets\n      │    │  ├─ If no intersection → Accept anyway (prefer aligned, allow misaligned)\n      │    │  └─ Record preferred affinity\n      │    │\n      │    └─ Policy: restricted\n      │       ├─ Find intersection of all hint sets\n      │       ├─ If no intersection → Reject pod (TopologyAffinityError)\n      │       └─ Only accept if all hints agree on NUMA assignment\n      │\n      ├─ 4. Return decision\n      │    ├─ Accept=true → Pod proceeds to scheduling\n      │    └─ Accept=false, Reason=\"TopologyAffinityError\" → Pod rejected\n      │\n      └─ 5. Record admission decision in topology manager state\n           └─ For later reference during actual container creation\n```\n\n**Topology Manager Implementation Evidence**:\n- File: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go`\n- Hint collection: Iterates hint providers via `AddHintProvider()` registrations\n- Policy enforcement: Separate `policy_*.go` files (`policy_none.go`, `policy_best_effort.go`, `policy_restricted.go`)\n- Scope handling: `scope_pod.go` for aggregating container hints at pod level\n\n### 3.4 Container Lifecycle Hooks\n\n**Entry Points**: `InternalContainerLifecycle` interface (`internal_container_lifecycle.go`)\n\nThe container manager provides lifecycle hooks called by the kubelet at key container points:\n\n#### A. Pre-Container Creation: `PreCreateContainer()`\n\nCalled before container creation to configure resource allocation:\n\n```\nPreCreateContainer(pod, container, containerConfig)\n  │\n  ├─ 1. CPU Manager: Get CPU assignment\n  │    ├─ cpuSet := cpuManager.GetCPUAffinity(pod.UID, container.Name)\n  │    └─ Set in containerConfig.CpusetCpus [cgroup cpuset.cpus]\n  │\n  ├─ 2. Memory Manager: Get NUMA assignment\n  │    ├─ numaNodes := memoryManager.GetMemoryAffinity(pod.UID, container.Name)\n  │    └─ Set in containerConfig.CpusetMems [cgroup cpuset.mems]\n  │\n  └─ 3. Return updated containerConfig to runtime\n       └─ Runtime creates container with these cpuset constraints\n```\n\n**Implementation**: `internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go` lines 1-100\n\n**Evidence**:\n- Lines 71-82: CPU Manager integration\n- Lines 83-91: Memory Manager integration\n- Container config populated before runtime call\n\n#### B. Pre-Container Start: `PreStartContainer()`\n\nCalled after container creation but before starting:\n\n```\nPreStartContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n  │\n  ├─ 1. CPU Manager: Record container and CPU assignment\n  │    └─ cpuManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n  │        └─ Writes to checkpoint file for recovery\n  │\n  ├─ 2. Memory Manager: Record container and NUMA assignment\n  │    └─ memoryManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n  │        └─ Writes to checkpoint file for recovery\n  │\n  └─ 3. Topology Manager: Track container assignment\n       └─ topologyManager.AddContainer(pod, container, containerID)\n           └─ Updates hint state for future pod admission decisions\n```\n\n#### C. Post-Container Stop: `PostStopContainer()`\n\nCalled after container termination:\n\n```\nPostStopContainer(containerID)\n  │\n  ├─ 1. Topology Manager: Clean up container state\n  │    └─ topologyManager.RemoveContainer(containerID)\n  │\n  ├─ 2. CPU Manager: Optional cleanup (state kept for checkpointing)\n  │\n  └─ 3. Memory Manager: Optional cleanup (state kept for checkpointing)\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 CPU Manager Failures\n\n**Scenario 1: Static CPU Policy, No Available CPUs**\n\nIf a pod requests exclusive CPUs but all reserved CPUs are exhausted:\n- Static policy cannot find contiguous CPU set\n- `AddContainer()` returns error\n- Pod container startup fails with `CPUManagerError`\n- **Pod remains in Pending state** until CPUs become available\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Resize pod request to non-exclusive CPUs\n- Scale down other exclusive pods\n- Requires manual intervention; no auto-remediation\n\n**Design Tradeoff**:\n- Static policy guarantees CPU isolation but can starve pods\n- `none` policy avoids starvation but no CPU affinity\n\n---\n\n**Scenario 2: Reconciliation Lag**\n\nIf a container escapes its assigned cpuset (due to container runtime bug or direct cgroup manipulation):\n- Reconciliation runs every 60s (default)\n- Container consumes CPUs for up to 60 seconds before move\n- **Fairness impact**: One pod can exceed its fair share\n\n**Design Decision**: Trade monitoring frequency for reduced lock contention on container manager\n\n---\n\n### 4.2 Memory Manager Failures\n\n**Scenario 1: NUMA Allocation Fails**\n\nIf memory manager cannot allocate memory on preferred NUMA nodes:\n- Static policy rejects the allocation\n- `AddContainer()` returns error\n- Pod cannot start\n\n**Scenario 2: Memory Overcommit**\n\nIf actual pod memory usage exceeds assigned limit:\n- Cgroup OOM killer terminates container\n- **Observed in practice**: BestEffort pods killed first due to OOM score (-999)\n- **Log evidence**: Container killed by OOM killer signal\n\n**Design Tradeoff**:\n- Cgroup v2 adds `memory.min` to protect high-priority tiers\n- Adds complexity but improves reliability\n\n---\n\n### 4.3 Topology Manager Admission Failures\n\n**Scenario: Topology Affinity Cannot Be Met**\n\nWith `restricted` policy, if CPU/Memory/Device hints have no intersection:\n\n```\nExample:\n  CPU Manager hints: NUMA node 0\n  Memory Manager hints: NUMA node 1\n  Device Manager hints: NUMA node 2\n\n  Intersection: empty\n  Policy: restricted\n  → Pod REJECTED with TopologyAffinityError\n```\n\n**Impact**: Valid resource requests rejected due to topology constraint mismatch\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Use `best-effort` policy to prefer aligned but accept misaligned\n- Adjust pod requests to align with available topology\n- Modify device plugin topology reporting\n\n**Design Tradeoff**:\n- `restricted` prevents performance-hurting misalignment (good for latency-sensitive workloads)\n- `best-effort` allows more schedules but degrades tail latency\n\n---\n\n### 4.4 Resource Quota Enforcement Limits\n\n**Hard Limits** (via CFS quota, memory.max):\n- CPU: Hard cap enforced by kernel CFS scheduler\n- Memory: Hard cap enforced by cgroup OOM killer\n- Cannot be violated; violations cause container termination\n\n**Soft Limits** (via CPU shares, memory.high):\n- CPU shares: Kernel guarantees proportional time, but doesn't hard-cap\n- Memory.high: Kernel reclaims memory via throttling, but allows temporary overage\n\n**Design Limit**: No intermediate guarantees between soft and hard; either pod gets CPU or doesn't\n\n---\n\n### 4.5 Cgroup Version Incompatibility\n\n**Cgroup v1 Issues** (Deprecated):\n- Multiple independent subsystems (cpu, memory, cpuset, pids)\n- More memory overhead per cgroup\n- Less precise memory accounting\n- **Warning logged** at startup: \"cgroup v1 detected. cgroup v1 support is deprecated...\"\n\n**Cgroup v2 Requirements**:\n- Kernel 5.4+ required for basic support\n- Kernel 5.8+ required for root `cpu.stat` (required for accurate CPU accounting)\n- **Code path**: Lines 52-59 in `container_manager.go` with kernel version checks\n\n**Design Decision**: Support both for backwards compatibility, but strongly encourage v2 migration\n\n---\n\n### 4.6 Platform-Specific Limits\n\n**Linux** (Full support):\n- All managers enabled: CPU, Memory, Topology, Device, DRA\n- Cgroup enforcement via cgroupfs\n\n**Windows** (Minimal support):\n- CPU Manager: Stub (no affinity)\n- Memory Manager: Stub\n- Topology Manager: Stub\n- Device Manager: Basic support only\n- Cgroup: Not available; relies on container runtime limits\n\n**Other Platforms** (Stub):\n- All managers return no-op stubs\n- No resource isolation beyond runtime defaults\n\n---\n\n### 4.7 Node Allocatable Enforcement Tradeoffs\n\n**Enforcement Goal**: Ensure `Node Allocatable = Node Capacity - Reserved`\n\n**Mechanism**:\n- Create cgroup at `kubepods` with resource limits\n- Force all pod cgroups under `kubepods`\n- Periodically enforce limits via cgroup manager updates\n\n**Challenge: Memory Overcommit** (lines 550-558):\n```\nIf actual pod memory usage > allocatable memory:\n  ├─ Reduce burstable tier limit (to free memory for guaranteed)\n  ├─ If still overcommitted, retry with increased frequency\n  └─ If unresolvable, log error but allow operation\n```\n\n**Design Tradeoff**:\n- Strict enforcement can crash workloads (OOM kill)\n- Permissive enforcement allows overcommit (performance degradation)\n- Kubernetes chose permissive: Log but don't kill\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: Extension Points, Customization Hooks, and Associated Risks\n\n### 5.1 CPU Manager Policy Customization\n\n**How to Add New Policy**:\n\n1. **Create policy file**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_custom.go`\n2. **Implement interface**:\n```go\ntype Manager interface {\n    Start(activePodsFunc) error\n    AddContainer(pod, container, containerID string) error\n    RemoveContainer(containerID string) error\n    GetCPUAffinity(podUID, containerName string) cpuset.CPUSet\n    // ... other methods\n}\n```\n3. **Register in NewManager()** (lines 80-100): Add case for policy name\n4. **Implement reconciliation** for crash recovery\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Allocation Deadlock**: If new policy exhausts CPUs, pods pending forever\n- **Data Corruption**: Checkpoint file format must match; incompatible format causes recovery failure\n- **Performance**: Static policy is O(N) search; complex policies could block container startup\n\n---\n\n### 5.2 Device Plugin Extension Points\n\n**Device Plugin Registration Flow**:\n\n```\nPlugin Manager watches: /var/lib/kubelet/device-plugins/\n  └─ Plugin creates Unix socket: example.sock\n      └─ Plugin registers with kubelet via gRPC\n          ├─ DevicePluginService.Register(pluginInfo)\n          └─ Passes back: ListAndWatchEndpoint, AllocateEndpoint\n```\n\n**Device Manager Integration**:\n- Location: `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go`\n- **ListAndWatch gRPC**: Stream device status (healthy/unhealthy)\n- **Allocate gRPC**: Called by container manager to allocate devices\n\n**Topology Hints Support**:\n- Plugin can report NUMA locality for each device\n- Device manager relays to topology manager during hint collection\n- Allows topology-aware device scheduling\n\n**Custom Hook Implementation**:\n```go\n// Device plugin implements\ntype DevicePlugin interface {\n    ListAndWatch(empty *Empty, stream DevicePlugin_ListAndWatchServer) error\n    Allocate(ctx context.Context, request *AllocateRequest) (*AllocateResponse, error)\n    PreStartContainer(ctx context.Context, request *PreStartContainerRequest) (*PreStartContainerResponse, error)\n    // ...\n}\n```\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Allocation Persistence**: Device allocation state lost if kubelet crashes (no checkpoint); devices might be double-allocated\n- **Plugin Crash**: If plugin crashes, allocated devices become orphaned; no auto-recovery\n- **Topology Mismatch**: If plugin reports inconsistent topology across calls, admission decisions become invalid\n\n---\n\n### 5.3 Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA) Driver Integration\n\n**DRA Manager** (`pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go`) provides hooks for custom resource drivers:\n\n```\nResourceClaim with ResourceClassName\n  ↓\nDRA Manager.PrepareDynamicResources(pod)\n  └─ For each ResourceClaim in pod:\n      ├─ Get ResourceDriver endpoint from ResourceClass\n      ├─ Call Driver.Prepare(claim) gRPC\n      ├─ Wait for ClaimStatus.AllocationResult\n      ├─ Return CDI device paths to container runtime\n      └─ Record claim state for unprepare\n```\n\n**Extension**: Resource drivers are fully custom gRPC services (outside kubelet)\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Claim Deadlock**: If driver never completes Prepare(), pod waits forever\n- **Resource Leak**: If driver crashes after Prepare() but before Unprepare(), resources become orphaned\n- **Unavailable Updates**: If driver later reports claim unavailable, kubelet must evict pod; no graceful migration\n\n---\n\n### 5.4 Topology Manager Policy Customization\n\n**How to Add New Policy**:\n\n1. **Create policy file**: `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy_custom.go`\n2. **Implement**:\n```go\ntype TopologyAwarePolicy interface {\n    Name() string\n    CanAdmitPodResult(*TopologyHints) *lifecycle.PodAdmitResult\n    GetTopologyHints(*Pod, *Container) []TopologyHint\n}\n```\n3. **Register in NewManager()**: Add case for policy name\n\n**Builtin Policies** and their characteristics:\n- `none`: Always admits (no affinity enforcement)\n- `best-effort`: Prefers alignment, accepts misalignment → **Most flexible**\n- `restricted`: Requires alignment → **Most strict**\n- `single-numa-node`: All containers in pod on single NUMA node → **Hardware-optimal**\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Starvation**: Overly strict policy might make clusters unschedulable\n- **Inconsistent Hints**: If hint providers disagree (e.g., Device Manager reports different topology than actual), policy enforcement fails\n- **State Corruption**: If topology manager state file corrupted, node becomes unbootable (cannot parse existing pod topology assignments)\n\n---\n\n### 5.5 QoS Reservation Customization\n\n**QoS Reservation Feature** (enabled via `--qos-reserved` flag):\n\n```go\n// Example: reserve 20% of memory for burstable tier\n--qos-reserved=memory=20%\n\n// Translates to:\nQOSReserved: {\n    v1.ResourceMemory: int64(20),\n}\n```\n\n**Mechanism** (in `qos_container_manager_linux.go`, lines 349-373):\n```\nNode Allocatable Memory = 32 GB\nGuaranteed Pods Memory = 10 GB\nQOS Reserved = 20%\n\n→ Burstable Tier Memory Limit = 32 - 10 - (32 * 20%) = 15.6 GB\n```\n\n**Risks**:\n- **Memory Underutilization**: If guaranteed pods never reach reservation, memory wasted\n- **No Enforcement**: This is advisory; burstable pods can still exceed if guaranteed under-utilized\n- **Percentage Interpretation**: Different administrators might interpret percentage differently (of total vs. of allocatable)\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Operational Implications\n\n### 6.1 Performance Considerations\n\n#### CPU Manager Overhead\n\n**Exclusive CPU Allocation** (static policy):\n- **Startup Latency**: O(N) search through available CPUs during `AddContainer()` → **10-50ms for large socket counts**\n- **Checkpoint I/O**: Write to disk on each container addition → **5-20ms per add**\n- **Reconciliation**: Periodic scan of all containers for escapes → **100-500ms per 60s cycle**\n\n**Mitigation**:\n- Use `none` policy if CPU isolation not critical\n- Increase reconciliation interval if I/O pressure high\n- Pre-reserve CPU sets to avoid fragmentation\n\n#### Memory Manager Overhead\n\n**NUMA Affinity Calculation** (static policy):\n- **Startup Latency**: Lookup NUMA topology and find compatible nodes → **5-20ms**\n- **Checkpoint I/O**: Write allocation state → **5-20ms**\n\n**Memory QoS** (cgroup v2):\n- **Per-Tier Updates**: Calculate and apply memory limits every 60s → **10-50ms per update**\n- **Additional Syscalls**: Setting memory.min, memory.high per-pod → Linear with pod count\n\n#### Topology Manager Latency\n\n**Hint Collection**:\n- For each pod, call GetTopologyHints() on all hint providers (CPU, Memory, Device managers)\n- With 3 managers, each taking 5-10ms → **Total 15-30ms per pod admission**\n- Serialized (not parallel), so scales linearly with managers\n\n**Policy Evaluation**:\n- best-effort/restricted: Intersection of NUMA node sets → **O(N*M) with N hints, M managers**\n- single-numa-node: Stricter evaluation → **O(N²) in worst case**\n\n#### Device Manager Latency\n\n**Device Allocation**:\n- gRPC call to device plugin `Allocate()` → **50-500ms depending on plugin implementation**\n- Plugin might contact external hardware → Additional latency\n\n**Critical Path**: Device plugin latency is on critical path for container startup\n\n---\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Failure Recovery\n\n#### Checkpoint-Based Recovery\n\n**CPU Manager Checkpoint** (`cpu_manager_state` file):\n```\nLocation: <kubelet-root>/cpu_manager_state\nFormat: JSON with container ID → CPUSet mapping\nPurpose: Recover allocations after kubelet crash\nLimitations: Cannot recover allocations for containers deleted before kubelet restart\n```\n\n**Recovery Process**:\n1. On start, load checkpoint\n2. Query runtime for running containers\n3. For each running container:\n   - If in checkpoint, restore CPU affinity\n   - If not in checkpoint, **reset cpuset to all CPUs** (loss of exclusive allocation)\n4. Reconcile every 60s to restore any escaped processes\n\n**Risk**: If checkpoint corrupted or lost, all exclusive CPU allocations forgotten\n\n---\n\n#### Device Plugin State Loss\n\n**No Checkpoint for Device Allocation**:\n- Device allocation state kept in memory\n- On kubelet crash, state lost\n- **Devices might be double-allocated if pod scheduled to another node**\n- **Design tradeoff**: Avoid I/O overhead for device state at cost of recovery safety\n\n**Mitigation**: External resource management (e.g., k8s resource reservations) should enforce uniqueness\n\n---\n\n#### Topology Manager State Loss\n\n**No Persistent State**:\n- Topology assignments kept in memory\n- On restart, all pods re-admitted via Admit() method\n- **Design decision**: Stateless readmission safer than corrupt state recovery\n- **Cost**: Admits only pods that currently exist (not past decisions)\n\n---\n\n### 6.3 Observability and Debugging\n\n#### Key Metrics\n\n**CPU Manager** (prometheus):\n- No official metrics (state internal)\n- **Observable via cgroups**: `cat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/cpuset.cpus`\n\n**Memory Manager**:\n- No official metrics\n- **Observable via cgroups**: `cat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/memory.usage_in_bytes`\n\n**Topology Manager**:\n- No official metrics\n- **Observable via logs**: \"Successfully admitted pod for topology policy\"\n\n**Device Manager**:\n- `kubelet_device_plugin_allocation_duration_seconds` histogram\n- `kubelet_device_plugin_request_total` counter\n- `kubelet_device_plugin_request_errors_total` counter\n\n#### Logging Evidence\n\n**CPU Manager Debug Logs** (`--v=4` or higher):\n```\n\"Container X has pinned cpus\"\n\"Successfully added container X to exclusive cpus\"\n\"Reconciling container assignments\"\n```\n\n**QoS Manager Logs**:\n```\n\"Updated QOS container cpushares\"\n\"Setting memory reserved\"\n\"MemoryQoS config for pod\"\n```\n\n**Topology Manager Logs**:\n```\n\"Successfully admitted pod for topology policy\"\n\"Pod rejected for topology policy: TopologyAffinityError\"\n```\n\n---\n\n#### Debugging Cgroups\n\n**Check pod cgroup hierarchy**:\n```bash\n# Guaranteed pod\nls /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods.guaranteed.podXXX/\n\n# Burstable pod\nls /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/\n\n# View CPU set\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpuset/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/cpuset.cpus\n\n# View memory limit\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/memory/kubepods.burstable.podXXX/memory.limit_in_bytes\n```\n\n**Check QoS tier limits**:\n```bash\n# Burstable tier CPU shares\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/kubepods.burstable/cpu.shares\n\n# BestEffort tier\ncat /sys/fs/cgroup/cpu/kubepods.besteffort/cpu.shares\n```\n\n---\n\n### 6.4 Node Allocatable Enforcement\n\n**Default Reservations**:\n- `kube-reserved`: CPU and memory reserved for kubelet, systemd, etc. (default none)\n- `system-reserved`: CPU and memory reserved for OS (default none)\n- `eviction-hard`: Thresholds for evicting pods (e.g., memory < 5%)\n\n**Effective Node Allocatable**:\n```\nAllocatable = Capacity - Kube-Reserved - System-Reserved\n```\n\n**Example**:\n```\nNode Capacity:     32 CPUs, 64 GB memory\nKube-Reserved:     2 CPUs, 4 GB memory\nSystem-Reserved:   1 CPU, 2 GB memory\n─────────────────────────────────────────\nNode Allocatable:  29 CPUs, 58 GB memory (reported to scheduler)\n```\n\n**Enforcement Mechanism** (lines 550-558 in `container_manager_linux.go`):\n- Root pod cgroup (`kubepods`) created with limits = allocatable\n- All user pods placed under `kubepods`\n- Periodic enforcement every 60s\n\n**Failure Scenario**: If actual pod usage > allocatable:\n- Memory OOM killer activates\n- BestEffort pods killed first (OOM score -999)\n- Guaranteed pods protected (OOM score 0 with systemd driver)\n- **Design decision**: Accept temporary overages rather than preemptively kill\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: Important Files and Directories Map\n\n### Core Container Manager\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager.go` - Main ContainerManager interface definition\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_linux.go` - Linux implementation with initialization and node setup\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/container_manager_windows.go` - Windows stub implementation\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/types.go` - CgroupManager, PodContainerManager, QOSContainersInfo interfaces\n\n### Cgroup Management\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_manager_linux.go` - Dispatcher selecting v1/v2 implementation\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v1_manager_linux.go` - Cgroup v1 filesystem-based implementation\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cgroup_v2_manager_linux.go` - Cgroup v2 unified hierarchy implementation\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/helpers_linux.go` - CPU/memory conversion helpers (MilliCPUToShares, etc.)\n\n### Pod and QoS Management\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/pod_container_manager_linux.go` - Pod-level cgroup creation and management\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/qos_container_manager_linux.go` - QoS tier (Guaranteed/Burstable/BestEffort) management\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/node_container_manager_linux.go` - Node-level container (root kubepods) setup\n\n### Container Lifecycle Hooks\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle.go` - InternalContainerLifecycle interface\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle_linux.go` - Linux implementation (CPU/memory pre-setup)\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/internal_container_lifecycle_windows.go` - Windows implementation\n\n### CPU Manager\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_manager.go` - Main CPU manager orchestrator\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy.go` - Policy interface\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_none.go` - No-op policy\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/policy_static.go` - Static exclusive CPU allocation\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/cpu_assignment.go` - CPU set calculations\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/state/state.go` - Checkpoint interface\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/cpumanager/state/state_checkpoint.go` - File-based persistence\n\n### Memory Manager\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/memory_manager.go` - Main memory manager\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy.go` - Policy interface\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/policy_none.go`, `policy_static.go`, `policy_best_effort.go` - Implementations\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/memorymanager/state/state_checkpoint.go` - Checkpoint persistence\n\n### Device Manager\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/manager.go` - Main device manager orchestrator\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/endpoint.go` - gRPC endpoint for device plugin communication\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/pod_devices.go` - Pod-to-device allocation tracking\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/topology_hints.go` - NUMA topology hint collection\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/devicemanager/checkpoint/checkpoint.go` - Device state persistence\n\n### Topology Manager\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/topology_manager.go` - Main topology manager\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy.go` - Policy interface\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/policy_none.go`, `policy_best_effort.go`, `policy_restricted.go` - Policy implementations\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/scope_pod.go` - Pod-scoped hint aggregation\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/topologymanager/numa_info.go` - NUMA topology representation\n\n### Dynamic Resource Allocation (DRA)\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/manager.go` - Main DRA manager for ResourceClaim handling\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/claiminfo.go` - Claim metadata storage\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/plugin/dra_plugin_manager.go` - Resource driver discovery and communication\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/dra/state/checkpointer.go` - Claim state persistence\n\n### Supporting Utilities\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/admission/` - Pod admission error types\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/containermap/` - Container UID to cgroup mapping\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/resourceupdates/updates.go` - Resource update event types (for device/claim status changes)\n- `pkg/kubelet/cm/testing/` - Mock implementations for testing\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Key Integration Points Summary\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n1. **Pod Spec** → Determines QoS class, resource requests/limits, device resource needs\n2. **Node Spec** → Provides capacity for allocation calculations\n3. **Active Pods Func** → Drives periodic reconciliation and QoS tier updates\n4. **Runtime Service** → Container execution notifications and status\n\n### Downstream Impacts\n1. **Container Runtime** → Pre-configured resource limits and cpuset constraints\n2. **Cgroup Filesystem** → Direct resource limit enforcement\n3. **Kubelet Status** → Resource allocations reported in pod status\n4. **Scheduler** → Topology hints influence pod placement decisions\n\n### Inter-Component Flows\n- **Topology Manager as Arbiter**: All resource-level decisions checked against topology policy\n- **QoS Manager as Enforcer**: Periodic tier-level updates regardless of individual pod lifecycle\n- **Device Manager as Bridge**: Translates plugin gRPC into kubelet resource constraints\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe kubelet container manager is a complex, multi-faceted subsystem that orchestrates resource allocation and enforcement across Linux cgroups, device plugins, and custom resource drivers. Its architecture achieves separation of concerns (CPU, Memory, Devices managed independently) while enforcing global constraints (topology affinity via topology manager, QoS fairness via QoS tiers). The tradeoffs between strict enforcement and operational flexibility, between comprehensive monitoring and performance, are consciously designed to prioritize pod stability over perfect fairness—a pragmatic choice for a diverse, multi-tenant platform.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

It provides:\n\n1. **Resource Isolation**: Prevents pods from exceeding allocated resources\n2. **QoS Enforcement**: Implements Kubernetes QoS tiers (Guaranteed, Burstable, BestEffort) with distinct CPU and memory behavior\n3. **Topology Optimization**: Aligns container resources to hardware topology (NUMA nodes) for optimal performance\n4. **Device Management**: Brokers extended resources (GPUs, accelerators) reported by device plugins\n5. **Admission Control**: Rejects pods that violate topology constraints before container creation\n6. **Node Accounting**: Tracks system resource consumption and ensures node allocatable is respected\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Upstream Dependencies** (What feeds into this subsystem):\n- **Pod Specification** (`v1.Pod`): CPU/memory requests and limits, QoS class, device plugin resource requests\n- **Node Specification** (`v1.Node`): Capacity, allocatable, extended resource counts\n- **Runtime Service** (`internalapi.RuntimeService`): Container startup notifications, actual container limits\n- **Active Pods Callback** (`ActivePodsFunc`): Current running pods for recalculation\n- **Plugin Manager**: Device plugin registration and health status\n\n**Downstream Consumers** (What this subsystem affects):\n- **Container Runtime** (CRI): Container execution with configured cpuset, memory limits via `RunContainerOptions`\n- **Cgroup Filesystem**: Direct manipulation via cgroup manager for resource limits\n- **Kubelet Status Module**: Pod resource status via `PodResources` API and allocated resources\n- **Scheduler Framework**: Topology hints inform scheduler pod placement decisions\n- **Kubelet Metrics**: CPU/memory usage from cAdvisor integration\n\n### Architectural Constraints\n\n- **Per-Node Scope**: Operates only on the local node; no inter-node coordination\n- **Immutable Pod QoS**: QoS class is determined once during pod creation based on requests/limits, not updated\n- **Best-Effort Reconciliation**: Periodic (1-minute) updates ensure desired vs. actual state;
